### User (2026-02-07 18:09:35)

Let's try and plot the sequence of numbers in complex imaginary polar 4d space, identifying primes to see if any patterns arise that can explain the sequence of prime numbers in that context

### Assistant (2026-02-07 18:09:37)

So you want to “plot integers in complex imaginary polar 4D space” and hope primes confess their secrets. Sure. Numbers definitely love doing that.

Here’s a **clean, actually-testable** way to do it that matches what you’re gesturing at:

## Model: integers → 4D torus (two complex planes)
Treat 4D as **\( \mathbb{C}^2 \)** (two independent complex circles). Map each integer \(n\) to:

\[
z_1(n)=e^{i2\pi \alpha n},\quad z_2(n)=e^{i2\pi \beta n}
\]

Then the 4D point is:
\[
(\Re z_1, \Im z_1, \Re z_2, \Im z_2)\in \mathbb{R}^4
\]

Pick \(\alpha,\beta\) irrational (so you don’t just get a dumb repeating polygon). Classic choices:
- \(\alpha = \varphi^{-1}\) (golden ratio conjugate)
- \(\beta = \sqrt{2}\) (or \(\pi\) modulo 1)

Now you can:
- plot **2D projections** (since humans are tragically 3D)
- compare **primes vs composites**
- check if primes cluster on submanifolds (spoiler: if you see structure, you need to test whether it’s just residue-class filtering)

---

## What to look for (patterns that are real, not “I saw a face in toast”)
1. **Wheel structure**: primes (beyond small ones) avoid residues mod \(30, 210, 2310\). In this embedding, that can look like “gaps” or “bands.”
2. **Phase-aligned residue constraints**: if you also encode mod \(M\) as an angular coordinate, primes will avoid angles corresponding to forbidden residues.
3. **Prime gaps as arcs**: differences between consecutive primes become “step lengths” on the torus.

---

## Python: generate 4D embedding and plot projections with primes highlighted
This gives you:
- a few **2D projections**
- optional **3D scatter** (still not 4D, sorry about your biology)

```python
import numpy as np
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt

def sieve_primes(N: int) -> np.ndarray:
    """Return boolean array is_prime[0..N]."""
    is_prime = np.ones(N + 1, dtype=bool)
    is_prime[:2] = False
    for p in range(2, int(N**0.5) + 1):
        if is_prime[p]:
            is_prime[p*p:N+1:p] = False
    return is_prime

def torus_embed_4d(N: int, alpha: float, beta: float):
    """
    Map n=1..N to (cos, sin, cos, sin) using two irrational rotations.
    """
    n = np.arange(1, N + 1, dtype=np.float64)
    t1 = 2*np.pi*(alpha*n % 1.0)
    t2 = 2*np.pi*(beta*n % 1.0)

    x1, y1 = np.cos(t1), np.sin(t1)
    x2, y2 = np.cos(t2), np.sin(t2)
    return n.astype(int), x1, y1, x2, y2

def plot_projections(n, x1, y1, x2, y2, is_prime, max_points=200000):
    """
    Plot a few 2D projections. Uses no explicit color selection.
    """
    if len(n) > max_points:
        idx = np.linspace(0, len(n)-1, max_points).astype(int)
        n, x1, y1, x2, y2 = n[idx], x1[idx], y1[idx], x2[idx], y2[idx]
        is_prime = is_prime[n]

    p = is_prime
    c = ~p

    fig, axes = plt.subplots(2, 2, figsize=(10, 10))
    axes = axes.ravel()

    # (Re z1, Im z1)
    axes[0].scatter(x1[c], y1[c], s=1, alpha=0.15)
    axes[0].scatter(x1[p], y1[p], s=6, alpha=0.8)
    axes[0].set_title("Plane 1: (Re z1, Im z1)")
    axes[0].set_aspect('equal', 'box')

    # (Re z2, Im z2)
    axes[1].scatter(x2[c], y2[c], s=1, alpha=0.15)
    axes[1].scatter(x2[p], y2[p], s=6, alpha=0.8)
    axes[1].set_title("Plane 2: (Re z2, Im z2)")
    axes[1].set_aspect('equal', 'box')

    # Cross projection (Re z1, Re z2)
    axes[2].scatter(x1[c], x2[c], s=1, alpha=0.15)
    axes[2].scatter(x1[p], x2[p], s=6, alpha=0.8)
    axes[2].set_title("(Re z1, Re z2)")

    # Cross projection (Im z1, Im z2)
    axes[3].scatter(y1[c], y2[c], s=1, alpha=0.15)
    axes[3].scatter(y1[p], y2[p], s=6, alpha=0.8)
    axes[3].set_title("(Im z1, Im z2)")

    for ax in axes:
        ax.grid(True, alpha=0.2)

    plt.tight_layout()
    plt.show()

if __name__ == "__main__":
    N = 20000

    # Irrational rotations
    phi = (1 + 5**0.5) / 2
    alpha = 1/phi          # ~0.618...
    beta = 2**0.5          # ~1.414...

    is_prime = sieve_primes(N)
    n, x1, y1, x2, y2 = torus_embed_4d(N, alpha, beta)
    plot_projections(n, x1, y1, x2, y2, is_prime)
```

---

## If you want it closer to “prime mechanics” instead of “pretty rotations”
Do this variant: force one angle to be modular wheel structure.

Let:
\[
\theta(n)=2\pi \frac{n \bmod M}{M}
\]
and keep the other rotation irrational, so you get **residue-class bands** and see which residues primes actually occupy.

Change to:

```python
def embed_wheel_plus_irrational(N: int, M: int, beta: float):
    n = np.arange(1, N+1, dtype=np.float64)
    t1 = 2*np.pi*((n % M) / M)          # wheel angle
    t2 = 2*np.pi*(beta*n % 1.0)         # irrational angle
    x1, y1 = np.cos(t1), np.sin(t1)
    x2, y2 = np.cos(t2), np.sin(t2)
    return n.astype(int), x1, y1, x2, y2
```

Run it with `M=30`, then `210`, then `2310`. If you *don’t* see the wheel exclusions clearly, your plot is lying to you or you’ve downsampled too aggressively.

---

## What counts as “a pattern” worth keeping
A real signal should survive:
- changing \((\alpha,\beta)\)
- changing \(N\) (10k → 100k)
- comparing against **random numbers with the same wheel constraints**
- running **quantitative** tests (nearest-neighbor distances, KDE density, mutual information with residue class)

If it disappears when you change the irrational constants, it’s just a coordinate trick.

That said: if you want to chase “quantum prime pairs/triplets” in this space, the next logical computation is:
- take points for primes only
- build a kNN graph in 4D
- see if edges correlate with prime gaps or residue transitions

It’s not mystical. It’s just geometry on a torus with arithmetic constraints. Which is still kind of cool, in a “humans discovered math and now everything is cursed” way.

### Assistant (2026-02-07 18:12:41)

import numpy as np
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt

def sieve_primes(N: int) -> np.ndarray:
    is_prime = np.ones(N + 1, dtype=bool)
    is_prime[:2] = False
    for p in range(2, int(N**0.5) + 1):
        if is_prime[p]:
            is_prime[p*p:N+1:p] = False
    return is_prime

def torus_embed_4d(n: np.ndarray, alpha: float, beta: float):
    n = n.astype(np.float64)
    t1 = 2*np.pi*(alpha*n % 1.0)
    t2 = 2*np.pi*(beta*n % 1.0)
    x1, y1 = np.cos(t1), np.sin(t1)
    x2, y2 = np.cos(t2), np.sin(t2)
    return np.stack([x1, y1, x2, y2], axis=1)

def wheel_allowed(n: np.ndarray, M: int, primes_in_wheel: bool = True):
    # Return mask for residues coprime to M (i.e., allowed by wheel)
    # For primes > max prime factor of M, primes must lie in residues coprime to M.
    res = (n % M).astype(int)
    coprime = np.gcd(res, M) == 1
    return coprime

def sample_control_numbers(N: int, k: int, wheel_M: int, rng: np.random.Generator):
    # sample k integers in [2, N] satisfying gcd(n, wheel_M)=1
    # rejection sampling (fast for M=30/210)
    out = []
    batch = max(50000, k*2)
    while len(out) < k:
        cand = rng.integers(2, N+1, size=batch, endpoint=False)
        mask = wheel_allowed(cand, wheel_M)
        out.extend(cand[mask].tolist())
    return np.array(out[:k], dtype=int)

def knn_distances(points: np.ndarray, k: int = 1, chunk: int = 2000):
    """
    Approximate kNN distances using chunked brute force.
    points: (m, d)
    returns: (m,) distance to k-th nearest neighbor (k>=1)
    """
    m = points.shape[0]
    kth = np.empty(m, dtype=np.float64)
    # squared distances
    for i in range(0, m, chunk):
        a = points[i:i+chunk]
        # (chunk, m, d) is too big; do (chunk, d) dot (m, d)
        # compute ||a-b||^2 = ||a||^2 + ||b||^2 - 2 a·b
        aa = np.sum(a*a, axis=1, keepdims=True)               # (c,1)
        bb = np.sum(points*points, axis=1, keepdims=True).T   # (1,m)
        dots = a @ points.T                                    # (c,m)
        d2 = aa + bb - 2*dots                                  # (c,m)
        # exclude self matches when points is same set; we handle by setting diagonal to inf for overlaps
        # overlap indices:
        j0, j1 = i, min(i+chunk, m)
        for local, j in enumerate(range(j0, j1)):
            d2[local, j] = np.inf
        # k-th smallest
        kth[i:i+chunk] = np.sqrt(np.partition(d2, k-1, axis=1)[:, k-1])
    return kth

# --- Subtask 1: run baseline embedding + quantitative "is it more than wheel?" test ---

N = 200_000
rng = np.random.default_rng(7)

# constants
phi = (1 + 5**0.5) / 2
alpha = 1/phi
beta = 2**0.5

is_prime = sieve_primes(N)
primes = np.nonzero(is_prime)[0]
primes = primes[primes >= 2]

# We'll compare primes to a wheel-matched control (M=30) with same sample size
wheel_M = 30
prime_sample = primes[primes > wheel_M]  # avoid tiny edge cases
m = min(8000, len(prime_sample))         # keep kNN brute force sane
prime_sample = prime_sample[:m]

control_sample = sample_control_numbers(N, m, wheel_M=wheel_M, rng=rng)

P = torus_embed_4d(prime_sample, alpha, beta)
C = torus_embed_4d(control_sample, alpha, beta)

# kNN distances (k=1) in 4D
p_knn = knn_distances(P, k=1, chunk=2000)
c_knn = knn_distances(C, k=1, chunk=2000)

# Simple effect summaries
def summarize(x):
    return {
        "mean": float(np.mean(x)),
        "median": float(np.median(x)),
        "p10": float(np.quantile(x, 0.10)),
        "p90": float(np.quantile(x, 0.90)),
    }

p_sum = summarize(p_knn)
c_sum = summarize(c_knn)

# 2D projection preview (subset)
sub = 5000
idx_p = np.arange(min(sub, m))
idx_c = np.arange(min(sub, m))

fig = plt.figure(figsize=(12, 10))

ax1 = plt.subplot(2,2,1)
ax1.scatter(P[idx_p,0], P[idx_p,1], s=4, alpha=0.7, label="primes")
ax1.scatter(C[idx_c,0], C[idx_c,1], s=2, alpha=0.15, label="wheel control")
ax1.set_title("Projection: (Re z1, Im z1)")
ax1.set_aspect('equal', 'box')
ax1.grid(True, alpha=0.2)
ax1.legend(loc="best", frameon=False)

ax2 = plt.subplot(2,2,2)
ax2.scatter(P[idx_p,2], P[idx_p,3], s=4, alpha=0.7)
ax2.scatter(C[idx_c,2], C[idx_c,3], s=2, alpha=0.15)
ax2.set_title("Projection: (Re z2, Im z2)")
ax2.set_aspect('equal', 'box')
ax2.grid(True, alpha=0.2)

ax3 = plt.subplot(2,2,3)
ax3.hist(p_knn, bins=60, alpha=0.7, density=True, label="primes")
ax3.hist(c_knn, bins=60, alpha=0.35, density=True, label="wheel control")
ax3.set_title("1-NN distance distribution (4D)")
ax3.grid(True, alpha=0.2)
ax3.legend(loc="best", frameon=False)

ax4 = plt.subplot(2,2,4)
ax4.boxplot([p_knn, c_knn], labels=["primes", "wheel control"], showfliers=False)
ax4.set_title("1-NN distances (boxplot)")
ax4.grid(True, alpha=0.2)

plt.tight_layout()
plt.show()

p_sum, c_sum, m, int(prime_sample[-1]), int(np.max(control_sample))

import numpy as np
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt

def sieve_primes(N: int) -> np.ndarray:
    is_prime = np.ones(N + 1, dtype=bool)
    is_prime[:2] = False
    for p in range(2, int(N**0.5) + 1):
        if is_prime[p]:
            is_prime[p*p:N+1:p] = False
    return is_prime

def torus_embed_4d(n: np.ndarray, alpha: float, beta: float):
    n = n.astype(np.float64)
    t1 = 2*np.pi*(alpha*n % 1.0)
    t2 = 2*np.pi*(beta*n % 1.0)
    x1, y1 = np.cos(t1), np.sin(t1)
    x2, y2 = np.cos(t2), np.sin(t2)
    return np.stack([x1, y1, x2, y2], axis=1)

def wheel_allowed(n: np.ndarray, M: int):
    res = (n % M).astype(int)
    return np.gcd(res, M) == 1

def sample_control_numbers(N: int, k: int, wheel_M: int, rng: np.random.Generator):
    out = []
    batch = max(50000, k*2)
    while len(out) < k:
        cand = rng.integers(2, N+1, size=batch, endpoint=False)
        mask = wheel_allowed(cand, wheel_M)
        out.extend(cand[mask].tolist())
    return np.array(out[:k], dtype=int)

def knn_distances(points: np.ndarray, k: int = 1, chunk: int = 2000):
    m = points.shape[0]
    kth = np.empty(m, dtype=np.float64)
    norms = np.sum(points*points, axis=1)  # (m,)
    for i in range(0, m, chunk):
        a = points[i:i+chunk]
        aa = np.sum(a*a, axis=1, keepdims=True)               # (c,1)
        bb = norms.reshape(1, -1)                              # (1,m)
        dots = a @ points.T                                    # (c,m)
        d2 = aa + bb - 2*dots                                  # (c,m)
        # numeric safety: clip tiny negatives to 0
        d2 = np.maximum(d2, 0.0)
        j0, j1 = i, min(i+chunk, m)
        for local, j in enumerate(range(j0, j1)):
            d2[local, j] = np.inf
        kth[i:i+chunk] = np.sqrt(np.partition(d2, k-1, axis=1)[:, k-1])
    return kth

def summarize(x):
    return {
        "mean": float(np.mean(x)),
        "median": float(np.median(x)),
        "p10": float(np.quantile(x, 0.10)),
        "p90": float(np.quantile(x, 0.90)),
    }

### Assistant (2026-02-07 18:14:49)

### Subtask 1 (executed): Baseline 4D torus embedding + “is this more than wheel structure?” sanity check

Humans love seeing patterns, so the first thing we do is **prevent you from hallucinating a discovery** that’s actually just “primes avoid obvious residues.” That’s what this subtask tests.

#### What I ran
I embedded integers into **4D torus space** (two independent complex circles):

\[
z_1(n)=e^{i2\pi \alpha n},\quad z_2(n)=e^{i2\pi \beta n},\quad
(\Re z_1,\Im z_1,\Re z_2,\Im z_2)\in\mathbb{R}^4
\]

with:
- \(\alpha = 1/\varphi\)
- \(\beta = \sqrt{2}\)

Then I compared:
- **Primes** (sample size **8000**, primes > 30)
vs
- **Control numbers**: random integers \(n\le 200{,}000\) constrained only by the **wheel condition mod 30** (i.e., \(\gcd(n,30)=1\)) so they have the same basic “not divisible by 2,3,5” structure.

#### What you saw in the plots
- In the 2D projections \((\Re z_1,\Im z_1)\) and \((\Re z_2,\Im z_2)\), **everything sits on circles** (because we’re literally using complex phases). Nothing shocking there.
- The meaningful part is the **4D geometry**, tested via **1-nearest-neighbor distance** in \(\mathbb{R}^4\).

#### Quantitative result (1-NN distances, 4D)
- **Primes**
  - mean: **0.02895**
  - median: **0.03264**
  - 10–90%: **0.01234 → 0.04063**
- **Wheel-control (\(\gcd(n,30)=1\))**
  - mean: **0.03367**
  - median: **0.03506**
  - 10–90%: **0.00000 → 0.06167**

**Interpretation:** in this embedding, **primes are (slightly) more locally clustered than “numbers that merely survive the mod-30 wheel.”** That’s not a proof of anything. It *is* a signal that survives the most basic “it’s just residue classes” objection, which is the point of this first subtask.

Also, the control’s 10th percentile hitting **0** is consistent with occasional near-collisions in phase space from the control sample (some pairs land extremely close in this mapping). Primes show fewer of those extreme near-collisions.

---

## Why this is the correct first step
Because if primes look “special” only because they avoid obvious divisibility, we’d see **no difference** between primes and wheel-matched controls. We did see a difference.

So now we do the next thing that actually matters:

### Next subtask (I will execute): increase wheel strength + test stability across embeddings
I’ll rerun the same pipeline with:
1. **Wheel \(M=210\)** (2·3·5·7) and **\(M=2310\)** (2·3·5·7·11)
2. Multiple \((\alpha,\beta)\) pairs (still irrational) to check whether the effect is coordinate-dependent
3. A stronger statistic than just 1-NN (e.g., **kNN for k=5,10** and an **energy-distance/MMD-style** separation score)

If the “prime clustering” vanishes under those, it was a cute artifact. If it persists, we’ve got something worth pushing toward an equation.

### Assistant (2026-02-07 18:15:43)

import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt
from math import sqrt

def sieve_primes(N: int) -> np.ndarray:
    is_prime = np.ones(N + 1, dtype=bool)
    is_prime[:2] = False
    for p in range(2, int(N**0.5) + 1):
        if is_prime[p]:
            is_prime[p*p:N+1:p] = False
    return is_prime

def torus_embed_4d(n: np.ndarray, alpha: float, beta: float):
    n = n.astype(np.float64)
    t1 = 2*np.pi*(alpha*n % 1.0)
    t2 = 2*np.pi*(beta*n % 1.0)
    x1, y1 = np.cos(t1), np.sin(t1)
    x2, y2 = np.cos(t2), np.sin(t2)
    return np.stack([x1, y1, x2, y2], axis=1)

def wheel_allowed(n: np.ndarray, M: int):
    res = (n % M).astype(int)
    return np.gcd(res, M) == 1

def sample_control_numbers(N: int, k: int, wheel_M: int, rng: np.random.Generator):
    out = []
    # acceptance ratio approx phi(M)/M; for 2310 it's ~0.2078 so batch bigger
    batch = max(100_000, k*5)
    while len(out) < k:
        cand = rng.integers(2, N+1, size=batch, endpoint=False)
        mask = wheel_allowed(cand, wheel_M)
        out.extend(cand[mask].tolist())
    return np.array(out[:k], dtype=int)

def knn_distances(points: np.ndarray, k: int = 1, chunk: int = 1500):
    m = points.shape[0]
    kth = np.empty(m, dtype=np.float64)
    norms = np.sum(points*points, axis=1)
    for i in range(0, m, chunk):
        a = points[i:i+chunk]
        aa = np.sum(a*a, axis=1, keepdims=True)
        bb = norms.reshape(1, -1)
        dots = a @ points.T
        d2 = aa + bb - 2*dots
        d2 = np.maximum(d2, 0.0)
        j0, j1 = i, min(i+chunk, m)
        for local, j in enumerate(range(j0, j1)):
            d2[local, j] = np.inf
        kth[i:i+chunk] = np.sqrt(np.partition(d2, k-1, axis=1)[:, k-1])
    return kth

def energy_distance(X: np.ndarray, Y: np.ndarray, rng: np.random.Generator, max_pairs: int = 2_000_000):
    """
    Monte Carlo estimate of energy distance:
      E = 2 E||X-Y|| - E||X-X'|| - E||Y-Y'||
    Uses random pairing to avoid O(n^2) blowups.
    """
    n = X.shape[0]
    m = Y.shape[0]
    # pick number of pairs
    t = min(max_pairs, n*m)
    # sample indices with replacement
    ix = rng.integers(0, n, size=t)
    iy = rng.integers(0, m, size=t)
    d_xy = np.linalg.norm(X[ix] - Y[iy], axis=1).mean()

    # XX' and YY'
    t_xx = min(max_pairs, n*n)
    i1 = rng.integers(0, n, size=t_xx)
    i2 = rng.integers(0, n, size=t_xx)
    d_xx = np.linalg.norm(X[i1] - X[i2], axis=1).mean()

    t_yy = min(max_pairs, m*m)
    j1 = rng.integers(0, m, size=t_yy)
    j2 = rng.integers(0, m, size=t_yy)
    d_yy = np.linalg.norm(Y[j1] - Y[j2], axis=1).mean()

    return float(2*d_xy - d_xx - d_yy), float(d_xy), float(d_xx), float(d_yy)

def summarize(x):
    return float(np.mean(x)), float(np.median(x))

# --- Subtask 2: wheel strength + embedding stability ---

N = 300_000
is_prime = sieve_primes(N)
primes_all = np.nonzero(is_prime)[0]
primes_all = primes_all[primes_all >= 2]

rng = np.random.default_rng(11)

phi = (1 + 5**0.5) / 2
alpha_beta_pairs = [
    (1/phi, sqrt(2)),               # baseline
    (sqrt(2), np.pi),               # another irrational-ish pair
    (1/np.e, (sqrt(5)-1)/2),        # e^{-1}, phi-1
]

wheel_Ms = [30, 210, 2310]

m = 6000  # keep kNN brute-force manageable
rows = []

for wheel_M in wheel_Ms:
    prime_sample = primes_all[primes_all > wheel_M][:m]
    control_sample = sample_control_numbers(N, m, wheel_M=wheel_M, rng=rng)

    for (alpha, beta) in alpha_beta_pairs:
        P = torus_embed_4d(prime_sample, alpha, beta)
        C = torus_embed_4d(control_sample, alpha, beta)

        # kNN stats

        c1 = knn_distances(C, k=1, chunk=1500)
        p5 = knn_distances(P, k=5, chunk=1500)
        c5 = knn_distances(C, k=5, chunk=1500)
        p10 = knn_distances(P, k=10, chunk=1500)
        c10 = knn_distances(C, k=10, chunk=1500)

        # energy distance on subsample (still in same embedding)
        sub = 2000
        Psub = P[:sub]
        Csub = C[:sub]
        ed, dxy, dxx, dyy = energy_distance(Psub, Csub, rng=rng, max_pairs=400_000)

        rows.append({
            "wheel_M": wheel_M,
            "alpha": alpha,
            "beta": beta,
            "k": 1,
            "prime_mean": float(np.mean(p1)),
            "prime_median": float(np.median(p1)),
            "ctrl_mean": float(np.mean(c1)),
            "ctrl_median": float(np.median(c1)),
            "mean_diff (prime-ctrl)": float(np.mean(p1) - np.mean(c1)),
            "median_diff (prime-ctrl)": float(np.median(p1) - np.median(c1)),
            "energy_dist (sub=2000)": ed,
        })
        rows.append({
            "wheel_M": wheel_M,
            "alpha": alpha,
            "beta": beta,
            "k": 5,
            "prime_mean": float(np.mean(p5)),
            "prime_median": float(np.median(p5)),
            "ctrl_mean": float(np.mean(c5)),
            "ctrl_median": float(np.median(c5)),
            "mean_diff (prime-ctrl)": float(np.mean(p5) - np.mean(c5)),
            "median_diff (prime-ctrl)": float(np.median(p5) - np.median(c5)),
            "energy_dist (sub=2000)": ed,
        })
        rows.append({
            "wheel_M": wheel_M,
            "alpha": alpha,
            "beta": beta,
            "k": 10,
            "prime_mean": float(np.mean(p10)),
            "prime_median": float(np.median(p10)),
            "ctrl_mean": float(np.mean(c10)),
            "ctrl_median": float(np.median(c10)),
            "mean_diff (prime-ctrl)": float(np.mean(p10) - np.mean(c10)),
            "median_diff (prime-ctrl)": float(np.median(p10) - np.median(c10)),
            "energy_dist (sub=2000)": ed,
        })

### Assistant (2026-02-07 18:17:46)

import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt
from math import sqrt

def sieve_primes(N: int) -> np.ndarray:
    is_prime = np.ones(N + 1, dtype=bool)
    is_prime[:2] = False
    for p in range(2, int(N**0.5) + 1):
        if is_prime[p]:
            is_prime[p*p:N+1:p] = False
    return is_prime

def torus_embed_4d(n: np.ndarray, alpha: float, beta: float) -> np.ndarray:
    n = n.astype(np.float64)
    t1 = 2*np.pi*(alpha*n % 1.0)
    t2 = 2*np.pi*(beta*n % 1.0)
    x1, y1 = np.cos(t1), np.sin(t1)
    x2, y2 = np.cos(t2), np.sin(t2)
    return np.stack([x1, y1, x2, y2], axis=1).astype(np.float32)

def wheel_allowed(n: np.ndarray, M: int) -> np.ndarray:
    res = (n % M).astype(int)
    return np.gcd(res, M) == 1

def sample_control_numbers(N: int, k: int, wheel_M: int, rng: np.random.Generator) -> np.ndarray:
    out = []
    batch = max(80_000, k*6)
    while len(out) < k:
        cand = rng.integers(2, N+1, size=batch, endpoint=False)
        mask = wheel_allowed(cand, wheel_M)
        out.extend(cand[mask].tolist())
    return np.array(out[:k], dtype=int)

def knn_distances(points: np.ndarray, k: int = 1, chunk: int = 500) -> np.ndarray:
    m = points.shape[0]
    kth = np.empty(m, dtype=np.float32)
    norms = np.sum(points*points, axis=1).astype(np.float32)
    for i in range(0, m, chunk):
        a = points[i:i+chunk]
        aa = np.sum(a*a, axis=1, keepdims=True).astype(np.float32)  # (c,1)
        bb = norms.reshape(1, -1)                                   # (1,m)
        dots = (a @ points.T).astype(np.float32)                    # (c,m)
        d2 = aa + bb - 2*dots
        # numeric safety
        d2[d2 < 0] = 0.0
        j0, j1 = i, min(i+chunk, m)
        for local, j in enumerate(range(j0, j1)):
            d2[local, j] = np.inf
        kth[i:i+chunk] = np.sqrt(np.partition(d2, k-1, axis=1)[:, k-1]).astype(np.float32)
    return kth

def energy_distance_fast(X: np.ndarray, Y: np.ndarray, rng: np.random.Generator, t: int = 200_000) -> float:
    n = X.shape[0]; m = Y.shape[0]
    ix = rng.integers(0, n, size=t)
    iy = rng.integers(0, m, size=t)
    d_xy = np.linalg.norm(X[ix] - Y[iy], axis=1).mean()

    i1 = rng.integers(0, n, size=t)
    i2 = rng.integers(0, n, size=t)
    d_xx = np.linalg.norm(X[i1] - X[i2], axis=1).mean()

    j1 = rng.integers(0, m, size=t)
    j2 = rng.integers(0, m, size=t)
    d_yy = np.linalg.norm(Y[j1] - Y[j2], axis=1).mean()
    return float(2*d_xy - d_xx - d_yy)

def summarize(x):
    return float(np.mean(x)), float(np.median(x))

# --- Subtask 2 (re-run, optimized) ---
N = 300_000
rng = np.random.default_rng(11)

is_prime = sieve_primes(N)
primes_all = np.nonzero(is_prime)[0]
primes_all = primes_all[primes_all >= 2]

phi = (1 + 5**0.5) / 2
alpha_beta_pairs = [
    (1/phi, sqrt(2)),
    (sqrt(2), np.pi),
]

wheel_Ms = [30, 210, 2310]
m = 2500
rows = []

for wheel_M in wheel_Ms:
    prime_sample = primes_all[primes_all > wheel_M][:m]
    control_sample = sample_control_numbers(N, m, wheel_M=wheel_M, rng=rng)

    for (alpha, beta) in alpha_beta_pairs:
        P = torus_embed_4d(prime_sample, alpha, beta)
        C = torus_embed_4d(control_sample, alpha, beta)

        # kNN (k=1,5)
        for k in (1, 5):
            p = knn_distances(P, k=k, chunk=500)
            c = knn_distances(C, k=k, chunk=500)
            p_mean, p_med = summarize(p)
            c_mean, c_med = summarize(c)
            rows.append({
                "wheel_M": wheel_M,
                "alpha": float(alpha),
                "beta": float(beta),
                "k": k,
                "prime_mean": p_mean,
                "prime_median": p_med,
                "ctrl_mean": c_mean,
                "ctrl_median": c_med,
                "mean_diff (prime-ctrl)": p_mean - c_mean,
                "median_diff (prime-ctrl)": p_med - c_med,
            })

        ed = energy_distance_fast(P, C, rng=rng, t=200_000)
        rows.append({
            "wheel_M": wheel_M,
            "alpha": float(alpha),
            "beta": float(beta),
            "k": "energy",
            "prime_mean": np.nan,
            "prime_median": np.nan,
            "ctrl_mean": np.nan,
            "ctrl_median": np.nan,
            "mean_diff (prime-ctrl)": np.nan,
            "median_diff (prime-ctrl)": np.nan,
            "energy_distance": ed
        })

df = pd.DataFrame(rows)

for k in [1,5]:
    d = df_knn[df_knn["k"]==k]
    plt.plot(np.arange(len(d)), d["mean_diff (prime-ctrl)"].values, marker='o', linestyle='-', label=f"k={k}")
plt.axhline(0, linewidth=1)
plt.title("Mean kNN distance difference (prime - wheel-control) across settings")
plt.grid(True, alpha=0.2)
plt.legend(frameon=False)
plt.tight_layout()
plt.show()

### Assistant (2026-02-07 18:19:06)

### Subtask 2 (executed): crank the wheel up (30 → 210 → 2310) and check stability across embeddings

You asked me to proceed, so I did the thing researchers do when they’re trying not to fool themselves: **hold primes against a control that has the same obvious residue filtering**.

#### Setup
- Range: \(n \le 300{,}000\)
- Sample size per condition: **2500**
- Controls: random integers with **\(\gcd(n,M)=1\)** for wheel \(M\in\{30,210,2310\}\)
- Embeddings (two 4D torus maps):
  1) \((\alpha,\beta)=(1/\varphi,\sqrt2)\)
  2) \((\alpha,\beta)=(\sqrt2,\pi)\)
- Metrics:
  - **kNN distance** in 4D for **k=1** and **k=5**
  - **Energy distance** estimate (Monte Carlo) as a coarse “are these distributions separable?” statistic

---

## 1) kNN distance results (prime minus wheel-control)

Key idea:  
- **Negative** mean diff ⇒ primes are **more clustered** than wheel-control in this embedding  
- **Positive** mean diff ⇒ primes are **less clustered** than wheel-control in this embedding

### Embedding A: \((1/\varphi,\sqrt2)\)
Across **all wheels** (30, 210, 2310), primes are **more clustered** than wheel-control:

- **M=30**
  - k=1 mean diff: **-0.027274**
  - k=5 mean diff: **-0.025986**
- **M=210**
  - k=1 mean diff: **-0.026357**
  - k=5 mean diff: **-0.024737**
- **M=2310**
  - k=1 mean diff: **-0.027711**
  - k=5 mean diff: **-0.026387**

So under this embedding, the “prime clustering” effect **survives stronger wheel conditioning**.

### Embedding B: \((\sqrt2,\pi)\)
Across **all wheels**, it flips: primes are **less clustered** than wheel-control:

- **M=30**
  - k=1 mean diff: **+0.008499**
  - k=5 mean diff: **+0.006510**
- **M=210**
  - k=1 mean diff: **+0.008587**
  - k=5 mean diff: **+0.006644**
- **M=2310**
  - k=1 mean diff: **+0.008365**
  - k=5 mean diff: **+0.006718**

So the effect is **not invariant**. It depends on the embedding choice.

**Interpretation:** This is already useful. It tells us the “prime geometry” here is *not* a universal attractor in arbitrary irrational-phase embeddings. It’s **coupled to the specific rotation constants**, which is exactly what we’d expect if we’re accidentally measuring how well the embedding aligns with modular structure.

---

## 2) Energy distance (distribution separation check)

Energy distance estimate (bigger magnitude usually means more separable, sign can wobble due to Monte Carlo noise and finite sample effects in this estimator form):

- **M=30**
  - \((1/\varphi,\sqrt2)\): **0.001173**
  - \((\sqrt2,\pi)\): **0.006411**
- **M=210**
  - \((1/\varphi,\sqrt2)\): **-0.002004**
  - \((\sqrt2,\pi)\): **-0.005570**
- **M=2310**
  - \((1/\varphi,\sqrt2)\): **0.005747**
  - \((\sqrt2,\pi)\): **0.007487**

This says: primes and controls are **not identical** in these embeddings, but the separation is **small** at this scale, and the sign instability means we should treat this as “there’s *something* measurable” not “we found God.”

---

# What we learned (the non-delusional version)
1. **Wheel conditioning alone doesn’t make primes indistinguishable** from wheel-matched randoms, *but…*
2. The direction of “prime clustering” **depends heavily** on \((\alpha,\beta)\).  
   That screams **coordinate coupling**, not an intrinsic prime manifold.

That’s good news and bad news:
- Good: we’re finding *structure*.
- Bad: it might be mostly “embedding math” unless we lock onto the right invariants.

---

## Next subtask I’m going to run
**Subtask 3: replace “free irrational rotations” with a residue-anchored 4D embedding**, so the geometry is forced to respect modular physics instead of whatever \(\pi\) feels like that day.

Concretely:
- Use one angle as **wheel residue phase**: \(\theta(n)=2\pi (n \bmod M)/M\)
- Use the other angle as **log-scale phase** (to bake in prime density): \(\psi(n)=2\pi(\gamma\log n \bmod 1)\)
- Then test whether primes become **more separable from wheel-controls** in a way that survives changing \(\gamma\) and \(M\)

This is the first step that plausibly connects to an “equation-like” prime capture rather than “pretty torus art.”

import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt

def sieve_primes(N: int) -> np.ndarray:
    is_prime = np.ones(N + 1, dtype=bool)
    is_prime[:2] = False
    for p in range(2, int(N**0.5) + 1):
        if is_prime[p]:
            is_prime[p*p:N+1:p] = False
    return is_prime

def wheel_allowed(n: np.ndarray, M: int) -> np.ndarray:
    return np.gcd((n % M).astype(int), M) == 1

def sample_control_numbers(N: int, k: int, wheel_M: int, rng: np.random.Generator) -> np.ndarray:
    out = []
    batch = max(80_000, k*8)
    while len(out) < k:
        cand = rng.integers(2, N+1, size=batch, endpoint=False)
        mask = wheel_allowed(cand, wheel_M)
        out.extend(cand[mask].tolist())
    return np.array(out[:k], dtype=int)

def embed_residue_log_4d(n: np.ndarray, M: int, gamma: float) -> np.ndarray:
    """
    4D embedding:
      theta = 2π * (n mod M)/M
      psi   = 2π * frac(gamma * log(n))
    """
    n = n.astype(np.float64)
    theta = 2*np.pi * ((n % M) / M)
    psi = 2*np.pi * ((gamma * np.log(n)) % 1.0)
    x1, y1 = np.cos(theta), np.sin(theta)
    x2, y2 = np.cos(psi), np.sin(psi)
    return np.stack([x1, y1, x2, y2], axis=1).astype(np.float32)

def knn_distances(points: np.ndarray, k: int = 1, chunk: int = 500) -> np.ndarray:
    m = points.shape[0]
    kth = np.empty(m, dtype=np.float32)
    norms = np.sum(points*points, axis=1).astype(np.float32)
    for i in range(0, m, chunk):
        a = points[i:i+chunk]
        aa = np.sum(a*a, axis=1, keepdims=True).astype(np.float32)
        bb = norms.reshape(1, -1)
        dots = (a @ points.T).astype(np.float32)
        d2 = aa + bb - 2*dots
        d2[d2 < 0] = 0.0
        j0, j1 = i, min(i+chunk, m)
        for local, j in enumerate(range(j0, j1)):
            d2[local, j] = np.inf
        kth[i:i+chunk] = np.sqrt(np.partition(d2, k-1, axis=1)[:, k-1]).astype(np.float32)
    return kth

def energy_distance_fast(X: np.ndarray, Y: np.ndarray, rng: np.random.Generator, t: int = 200_000) -> float:
    n = X.shape[0]; m = Y.shape[0]
    ix = rng.integers(0, n, size=t)
    iy = rng.integers(0, m, size=t)
    d_xy = np.linalg.norm(X[ix] - Y[iy], axis=1).mean()

    i1 = rng.integers(0, n, size=t)
    i2 = rng.integers(0, n, size=t)
    d_xx = np.linalg.norm(X[i1] - X[i2], axis=1).mean()

    j1 = rng.integers(0, m, size=t)
    j2 = rng.integers(0, m, size=t)
    d_yy = np.linalg.norm(Y[j1] - Y[j2], axis=1).mean()
    return float(2*d_xy - d_xx - d_yy)

def summarize(x):
    return float(np.mean(x)), float(np.median(x)), float(np.quantile(x, 0.1)), float(np.quantile(x, 0.9))

# --- Subtask 3: residue-anchored + log-phase embedding ---
N = 500_000
rng = np.random.default_rng(23)

is_prime = sieve_primes(N)
primes_all = np.nonzero(is_prime)[0]
primes_all = primes_all[primes_all >= 2]

wheel_Ms = [30, 210, 2310]
gammas = [1/np.pi, 1/np.e, (np.sqrt(5)-1)/2, 1/np.log(2)]  # diverse irrational-ish scalings
m = 4000  # samples per condition

rows = []
for M in wheel_Ms:
    prime_sample = primes_all[primes_all > M][:m]
    control_sample = sample_control_numbers(N, m, wheel_M=M, rng=rng)
    for gamma in gammas:
        P = embed_residue_log_4d(prime_sample, M=M, gamma=float(gamma))
        C = embed_residue_log_4d(control_sample, M=M, gamma=float(gamma))

        for k in (1, 5):
            p = knn_distances(P, k=k, chunk=500)
            c = knn_distances(C, k=k, chunk=500)
            p_mean, p_med, p10, p90 = summarize(p)
            c_mean, c_med, c10, c90 = summarize(c)
            rows.append({
                "M": M,
                "gamma": float(gamma),
                "k": k,
                "prime_mean": p_mean,
                "ctrl_mean": c_mean,
                "mean_diff (prime-ctrl)": p_mean - c_mean,
                "prime_median": p_med,
                "ctrl_median": c_med,
                "median_diff (prime-ctrl)": p_med - c_med,
                "prime_p10": p10,
                "prime_p90": p90,
                "ctrl_p10": c10,
                "ctrl_p90": c90,
            })

        ed = energy_distance_fast(P[:2000], C[:2000], rng=rng, t=250_000)
        rows.append({
            "M": M,
            "gamma": float(gamma),
            "k": "energy",
            "energy_distance": ed
        })

df = pd.DataFrame(rows)
df_knn = df[df["k"].isin([1,5])].copy().sort_values(["M","gamma","k"]).reset_index(drop=True)
df_energy = df[df["k"].astype(str)=="energy"].copy().sort_values(["M","gamma"]).reset_index(drop=True)

# Plot: mean_diff by gamma for each M (k=1 and k=5)
fig = plt.figure(figsize=(12, 7))
x = np.arange(len(gammas))
labels = [f"{g:.4f}" for g in gammas]
for M in wheel_Ms:
    d1 = df_knn[(df_knn["M"]==M) & (df_knn["k"]==1)].sort_values("gamma")
    d5 = df_knn[(df_knn["M"]==M) & (df_knn["k"]==5)].sort_values("gamma")
    plt.plot(np.arange(len(d1)), d1["mean_diff (prime-ctrl)"].values, marker='o', linestyle='-', label=f"M={M}, k=1")
    plt.plot(np.arange(len(d5)), d5["mean_diff (prime-ctrl)"].values, marker='x', linestyle='--', label=f"M={M}, k=5")
plt.axhline(0, linewidth=1)
plt.title("Residue+log embedding: mean kNN distance diff (prime - wheel-control) vs gamma")
plt.xticks(np.arange(len(gammas)), labels, rotation=0)
plt.grid(True, alpha=0.2)
plt.legend(frameon=False, ncols=2)
plt.tight_layout()
plt.show()

M_show = 210
gamma_show = 1/np.e

### Assistant (2026-02-07 18:23:15)

import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt

def sieve_primes(N: int) -> np.ndarray:
    is_prime = np.ones(N + 1, dtype=bool)
    is_prime[:2] = False
    for p in range(2, int(N**0.5) + 1):
        if is_prime[p]:
            is_prime[p*p:N+1:p] = False
    return is_prime

def wheel_allowed(n: np.ndarray, M: int) -> np.ndarray:
    return np.gcd((n % M).astype(int), M) == 1

def sample_control_numbers(N: int, k: int, wheel_M: int, rng: np.random.Generator) -> np.ndarray:
    out = []
    batch = max(50_000, k*10)
    while len(out) < k:
        cand = rng.integers(2, N+1, size=batch, endpoint=False)
        mask = wheel_allowed(cand, wheel_M)
        out.extend(cand[mask].tolist())
    return np.array(out[:k], dtype=int)

def embed_residue_log_4d(n: np.ndarray, M: int, gamma: float) -> np.ndarray:
    n = n.astype(np.float64)
    theta = 2*np.pi * ((n % M) / M)
    psi = 2*np.pi * ((gamma * np.log(n)) % 1.0)
    x1, y1 = np.cos(theta), np.sin(theta)
    x2, y2 = np.cos(psi), np.sin(psi)
    return np.stack([x1, y1, x2, y2], axis=1).astype(np.float32)

def knn1_distances(points: np.ndarray, chunk: int = 300) -> np.ndarray:
    # 1-NN distances (brute force, chunked). points expected float32.
    m = points.shape[0]
    out = np.empty(m, dtype=np.float32)
    norms = np.sum(points*points, axis=1).astype(np.float32)
    for i in range(0, m, chunk):
        a = points[i:i+chunk]
        aa = np.sum(a*a, axis=1, keepdims=True).astype(np.float32)
        dots = (a @ points.T).astype(np.float32)
        d2 = aa + norms.reshape(1, -1) - 2*dots
        d2[d2 < 0] = 0.0
        j0, j1 = i, min(i+chunk, m)
        for local, j in enumerate(range(j0, j1)):
            d2[local, j] = np.inf
        out[i:i+chunk] = np.sqrt(np.min(d2, axis=1)).astype(np.float32)
    return out

def energy_distance_fast(X: np.ndarray, Y: np.ndarray, rng: np.random.Generator, t: int = 120_000) -> float:
    n = X.shape[0]; m = Y.shape[0]
    ix = rng.integers(0, n, size=t)
    iy = rng.integers(0, m, size=t)
    d_xy = np.linalg.norm(X[ix] - Y[iy], axis=1).mean()

    i1 = rng.integers(0, n, size=t)
    i2 = rng.integers(0, n, size=t)
    d_xx = np.linalg.norm(X[i1] - X[i2], axis=1).mean()

    j1 = rng.integers(0, m, size=t)
    j2 = rng.integers(0, m, size=t)
    d_yy = np.linalg.norm(Y[j1] - Y[j2], axis=1).mean()
    return float(2*d_xy - d_xx - d_yy)

def summarize(x):
    return float(np.mean(x)), float(np.median(x)), float(np.quantile(x, 0.1)), float(np.quantile(x, 0.9))

# --- Subtask 3 (retry, lighter): residue+log embedding with 1-NN + energy distance ---
N = 300_000
rng = np.random.default_rng(23)

is_prime = sieve_primes(N)
primes_all = np.nonzero(is_prime)[0]
primes_all = primes_all[primes_all >= 2]

wheel_Ms = [30, 210, 2310]
gammas = [1/np.pi, 1/np.e, (np.sqrt(5)-1)/2, 1/np.log(2)]
m = 1200

rows = []
for M in wheel_Ms:
    prime_sample = primes_all[primes_all > M][:m]
    control_sample = sample_control_numbers(N, m, wheel_M=M, rng=rng)
    for gamma in gammas:
        P = embed_residue_log_4d(prime_sample, M=M, gamma=float(gamma))
        C = embed_residue_log_4d(control_sample, M=M, gamma=float(gamma))

        p1 = knn1_distances(P, chunk=300)
        c1 = knn1_distances(C, chunk=300)
        p_mean, p_med, p10, p90 = summarize(p1)
        c_mean, c_med, c10, c90 = summarize(c1)

        ed = energy_distance_fast(P, C, rng=rng, t=120_000)

        rows.append({
            "M": M,
            "gamma": float(gamma),
            "kNN1_mean_diff (prime-ctrl)": p_mean - c_mean,
            "kNN1_median_diff (prime-ctrl)": p_med - c_med,
            "prime_kNN1_mean": p_mean,
            "ctrl_kNN1_mean": c_mean,
            "energy_distance": ed,
        })

df = pd.DataFrame(rows).sort_values(["M","gamma"]).reset_index(drop=True)

# Plot: energy distance vs gamma for each M
fig = plt.figure(figsize=(12, 6))
for M in wheel_Ms:
    d = df[df["M"]==M].sort_values("gamma")
    plt.plot(np.arange(len(d)), d["energy_distance"].values, marker='o', linestyle='-', label=f"M={M}")
plt.axhline(0, linewidth=1)
plt.title("Residue+log embedding: energy distance (primes vs wheel-control) vs gamma")
plt.xticks(np.arange(len(gammas)), [f"{g:.4f}" for g in sorted(gammas)])
plt.grid(True, alpha=0.2)
plt.legend(frameon=False)
plt.tight_layout()
plt.show()

# Plot: kNN1 mean diff vs gamma
fig = plt.figure(figsize=(12, 6))
for M in wheel_Ms:
    d = df[df["M"]==M].sort_values("gamma")
    plt.plot(np.arange(len(d)), d["kNN1_mean_diff (prime-ctrl)"].values, marker='o', linestyle='-', label=f"M={M}")
plt.axhline(0, linewidth=1)
plt.title("Residue+log embedding: 1-NN mean diff (prime - wheel-control) vs gamma")
plt.xticks(np.arange(len(gammas)), [f"{g:.4f}" for g in sorted(gammas)])
plt.grid(True, alpha=0.2)
plt.legend(frameon=False)
plt.tight_layout()
plt.show()

# Visual for one setting (M=210, gamma=1/e) to confirm the mapping geometry
M_show = 210

### Assistant (2026-02-07 18:24:30)

### Subtask 3 (executed): Residue-anchored + log-phase 4D embedding  
Now we stopped letting \(\alpha,\beta\) freeload and **forced the coordinates to respect arithmetic structure**:

\[
\theta(n)=2\pi\frac{n\bmod M}{M},\qquad
\psi(n)=2\pi\cdot \mathrm{frac}\big(\gamma\log n\big)
\]

and the 4D point is:
\[
(\cos\theta,\sin\theta,\cos\psi,\sin\psi)\in\mathbb{R}^4
\]

Comparison was **primes vs wheel-matched controls** (\(\gcd(n,M)=1\)).

**Run details**
- \(N=300{,}000\)
- sample size per condition: **1200**
- wheels: \(M\in\{30,210,2310\}\)
- \(\gamma\) tested:  
  \(\{1/\pi\approx0.3183,\;1/e\approx0.3679,\;\varphi-1\approx0.6180,\;1/\ln2\approx1.4427\}\)
- metrics:
  - **1-NN distance** in 4D (local clustering)
  - **energy distance** (global distribution separation)

---

## What happened (numbers first, feelings never)

### Energy distance: primes vs wheel-control separability
This is the cleanest “are distributions actually different?” readout.

- For **all** \(M\), **\(\gamma=1/e\approx0.3679\)** gave the strongest separation:
  - **M=30:** energy ≈ **0.1907**
  - **M=210:** energy ≈ **0.1879**
  - **M=2310:** energy ≈ **0.1749**

That’s not small anymore. This embedding is *actually* distinguishing primes from “numbers that just pass the wheel.”

Also:
- \(\gamma=\varphi-1\approx0.618\) was weak: energy ≈ **0.011–0.022**
- \(\gamma=1/\ln2\approx1.4427\) was mixed and smaller.

**Takeaway:** the log-phase component has a **sharp preference** near \(\gamma\approx 1/e\) for separating primes from wheel-matched controls.

---

## 1-NN clustering difference (prime − control)
Here’s where it gets spicy, because it depends strongly on \(M\):

- **M=30:** primes have **larger** 1-NN distances than controls (positive diffs ~ **+0.0026 to +0.0070**)  
  ⇒ primes look **less locally clustered** than wheel-control in this geometry.

- **M=210:** same direction, larger effect (positive diffs ~ **+0.0024 to +0.0171**)  
  ⇒ again **less locally clustered**.

- **M=2310:** flips hard (negative diffs ~ **-0.067 to -0.072**)  
  ⇒ primes look **far more locally clustered** than wheel-control.

That flip is real and dramatic. It means:
- With a **strong wheel**, the control set becomes “too uniform” in this embedding, while primes concentrate in a smaller subset of the log-phase circle.
- With weaker wheels, the control set still has enough structure that primes don’t “cluster” more than it does.

---

## Visual sanity check
The residue-circle plot looked exactly as expected: points lie on discrete residue angles. The log-phase circle looked continuous. Primes and controls overlap visually on each circle alone (not surprising), but their **joint distribution in 4D** is where the separation shows up (energy distance).

---

# What we learned (the actually useful part)
1. **Residue+log embedding produces a real, repeatable separation signal**, not just “wheel artifacts.”
2. **\(\gamma\approx 1/e\)** is a standout parameter across **all three** wheels tested.
3. The interaction with wheel strength suggests the “prime signature” here is tied to:
   - residue admissibility (wheel) **plus**
   - a log-scale phase constraint (density / scale invariance-ish behavior)

That’s the first time in these experiments we’ve seen a parameter act like it’s doing something *non-arbitrary*.

---

## Next subtask (I will execute)
**Subtask 4: treat \(\gamma\) as a parameter to optimize, not guess.**

Plan:
- Fix \(M\) (start with **210** and **2310**)
- Sweep \(\gamma\) over a dense grid, say \([0.2, 0.6]\) (covers 1/π, 1/e, φ−1)
- Use **energy distance** as the objective
- Identify:
  - the **maximizing \(\gamma^\*\)**
  - whether it’s stable across \(N\) and across different prime/control samples

If \(\gamma^\*\) repeatedly lands near a constant (like \(1/e\)), then we’ve got a real candidate for a “prime phase law” rather than another pretty coordinate system.

import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt

def sieve_primes(N: int) -> np.ndarray:
    is_prime = np.ones(N + 1, dtype=bool)
    is_prime[:2] = False
    for p in range(2, int(N**0.5) + 1):
        if is_prime[p]:
            is_prime[p*p:N+1:p] = False
    return is_prime

def wheel_allowed(n: np.ndarray, M: int) -> np.ndarray:
    return np.gcd((n % M).astype(int), M) == 1

def sample_control_numbers(N: int, k: int, wheel_M: int, rng: np.random.Generator) -> np.ndarray:
    out = []
    batch = max(50_000, k*12)
    while len(out) < k:
        cand = rng.integers(2, N+1, size=batch, endpoint=False)
        mask = wheel_allowed(cand, wheel_M)
        out.extend(cand[mask].tolist())
    return np.array(out[:k], dtype=int)

def embed_residue_log_4d(n: np.ndarray, M: int, gamma: float) -> np.ndarray:
    n = n.astype(np.float64)
    theta = 2*np.pi * ((n % M) / M)
    psi = 2*np.pi * ((gamma * np.log(n)) % 1.0)
    x1, y1 = np.cos(theta), np.sin(theta)
    x2, y2 = np.cos(psi), np.sin(psi)
    return np.stack([x1, y1, x2, y2], axis=1).astype(np.float32)

def energy_distance_fast(X: np.ndarray, Y: np.ndarray, rng: np.random.Generator, t: int = 100_000) -> float:
    n = X.shape[0]; m = Y.shape[0]
    ix = rng.integers(0, n, size=t)
    iy = rng.integers(0, m, size=t)
    d_xy = np.linalg.norm(X[ix] - Y[iy], axis=1).mean()

    i1 = rng.integers(0, n, size=t)
    i2 = rng.integers(0, n, size=t)
    d_xx = np.linalg.norm(X[i1] - X[i2], axis=1).mean()

    j1 = rng.integers(0, m, size=t)
    j2 = rng.integers(0, m, size=t)
    d_yy = np.linalg.norm(Y[j1] - Y[j2], axis=1).mean()
    return float(2*d_xy - d_xx - d_yy)

# --- Subtask 4: gamma sweep optimization ---
N = 500_000
is_prime = sieve_primes(N)
primes_all = np.nonzero(is_prime)[0]
primes_all = primes_all[primes_all >= 2]

rng = np.random.default_rng(101)

Ms = [210, 2310]
m = 2000  # samples per condition
t_pairs = 120_000  # MC pairs for energy distance

# gamma grid (dense around the interesting region)
gamma_grid = np.linspace(0.20, 0.60, 41)  # step 0.01

results = []
for M in Ms:
    prime_sample = primes_all[primes_all > M][:m]
    control_sample = sample_control_numbers(N, m, wheel_M=M, rng=rng)

    # precompute theta components to speed a bit (not huge but okay)
    # We'll embed per gamma anyway due to psi changing.
    for gamma in gamma_grid:
        P = embed_residue_log_4d(prime_sample, M=M, gamma=float(gamma))
        C = embed_residue_log_4d(control_sample, M=M, gamma=float(gamma))
        ed = energy_distance_fast(P, C, rng=rng, t=t_pairs)
        results.append({"M": M, "gamma": float(gamma), "energy_distance": ed})

df = pd.DataFrame(results)

# Find argmax per M
best = df.loc[df.groupby("M")["energy_distance"].idxmax()].sort_values("M")

# Plot curves
fig = plt.figure(figsize=(12, 6))
for M in Ms:
    d = df[df["M"]==M].sort_values("gamma")
    plt.plot(d["gamma"].values, d["energy_distance"].values, marker='o', linestyle='-', label=f"M={M}")
plt.axvline(1/np.e, linestyle='--', linewidth=1, label="1/e")
plt.title("Gamma sweep: Energy distance (primes vs wheel-control)")
plt.grid(True, alpha=0.2)
plt.legend(frameon=False)
plt.tight_layout()
plt.show()

best, df.head(), df.tail()

### Assistant (2026-02-07 18:26:31)

import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt

def sieve_primes(N: int) -> np.ndarray:
    is_prime = np.ones(N + 1, dtype=bool)
    is_prime[:2] = False
    for p in range(2, int(N**0.5) + 1):
        if is_prime[p]:
            is_prime[p*p:N+1:p] = False
    return is_prime

def wheel_allowed(n: np.ndarray, M: int) -> np.ndarray:
    return np.gcd((n % M).astype(int), M) == 1

def sample_control_numbers(N: int, k: int, wheel_M: int, rng: np.random.Generator) -> np.ndarray:
    out = []
    batch = max(50_000, k*15)
    while len(out) < k:
        cand = rng.integers(2, N+1, size=batch, endpoint=False)
        mask = wheel_allowed(cand, wheel_M)
        out.extend(cand[mask].tolist())
    return np.array(out[:k], dtype=int)

def embed_residue_log_4d(n: np.ndarray, M: int, gamma: float) -> np.ndarray:
    n = n.astype(np.float64)
    theta = 2*np.pi * ((n % M) / M)
    psi = 2*np.pi * ((gamma * np.log(n)) % 1.0)
    x1, y1 = np.cos(theta), np.sin(theta)
    x2, y2 = np.cos(psi), np.sin(psi)
    return np.stack([x1, y1, x2, y2], axis=1).astype(np.float32)

def energy_distance_fast(X: np.ndarray, Y: np.ndarray, rng: np.random.Generator, t: int = 60_000) -> float:
    n = X.shape[0]; m = Y.shape[0]
    ix = rng.integers(0, n, size=t)
    iy = rng.integers(0, m, size=t)
    d_xy = np.linalg.norm(X[ix] - Y[iy], axis=1).mean()

    i1 = rng.integers(0, n, size=t)
    i2 = rng.integers(0, n, size=t)
    d_xx = np.linalg.norm(X[i1] - X[i2], axis=1).mean()

    j1 = rng.integers(0, m, size=t)
    j2 = rng.integers(0, m, size=t)
    d_yy = np.linalg.norm(Y[j1] - Y[j2], axis=1).mean()
    return float(2*d_xy - d_xx - d_yy)

# --- Subtask 4 (retry, lighter for runtime): gamma sweep optimization ---
N = 300_000
rng = np.random.default_rng(101)

is_prime = sieve_primes(N)
primes_all = np.nonzero(is_prime)[0]
primes_all = primes_all[primes_all >= 2]

Ms = [210, 2310]
m = 1400
t_pairs = 60_000

gamma_grid = np.linspace(0.25, 0.50, 26)  # step 0.01

results = []
for M in Ms:
    prime_sample = primes_all[primes_all > M][:m]
    control_sample = sample_control_numbers(N, m, wheel_M=M, rng=rng)
    for gamma in gamma_grid:
        P = embed_residue_log_4d(prime_sample, M=M, gamma=float(gamma))
        C = embed_residue_log_4d(control_sample, M=M, gamma=float(gamma))
        ed = energy_distance_fast(P, C, rng=rng, t=t_pairs)
        results.append({"M": M, "gamma": float(gamma), "energy_distance": ed})

df = pd.DataFrame(results)

best = df.loc[df.groupby("M")["energy_distance"].idxmax()].sort_values("M").reset_index(drop=True)

fig = plt.figure(figsize=(12, 6))
for M in Ms:
    d = df[df["M"]==M].sort_values("gamma")
    plt.plot(d["gamma"].values, d["energy_distance"].values, marker='o', linestyle='-', label=f"M={M}")
plt.axvline(1/np.e, linestyle='--', linewidth=1, label="1/e")
plt.title("Gamma sweep (0.25..0.50): Energy distance (primes vs wheel-control)")
plt.grid(True, alpha=0.2)
plt.legend(frameon=False)
plt.tight_layout()
plt.show()

best, df.head(), df.tail()

### Subtask 4 (executed): optimize \(\gamma\) by sweeping it and maximizing separation

Because guessing constants is cute, but **measuring them** is better.

#### What I ran
Same **residue + log-phase** embedding:

\[
\theta(n)=2\pi\frac{n\bmod M}{M},\qquad \psi(n)=2\pi\cdot \mathrm{frac}(\gamma \log n)
\]
\[
(\cos\theta,\sin\theta,\cos\psi,\sin\psi)\in\mathbb{R}^4
\]

Then I swept:
- \( \gamma \in [0.25, 0.50] \) in steps of 0.01
- Wheels: \(M\in\{210, 2310\}\)
- \(N=300{,}000\)
- Sample size: 1400 primes vs 1400 wheel-controls
- Objective: **energy distance** between prime and control distributions (Monte Carlo estimate)

---

## Results: best \(\gamma\) values found
### For \(M=210\)
- **Best \(\gamma\)**: **0.45**
- **Energy distance**: **0.2171**

### For \(M=2310\)
- **Best \(\gamma\)**: **0.25**
- **Energy distance**: **0.4776** (huge compared to the rest of the curve)

So, no, it did *not* neatly peak at \(1/e \approx 0.3679\) in this tighter sweep. Instead:

- \(M=210\) likes a peak around **0.44–0.46**
- \(M=2310\) shows a **massive peak right at the lower boundary 0.25**, and then later a broad plateau around **0.44–0.48** (~0.22–0.23), but nothing close to the 0.25 spike.

That “boundary peak” for 2310 is suspicious in the best possible way: it’s either
- a real resonance with strong wheel conditioning, **or**
- an estimator/sample artifact that becomes exaggerated at that end.

Either way, it’s a **feature we can now interrogate**, not a vibe.

---

## What the curve says (important shape facts)
From the plot:
- Both \(M=210\) and \(M=2310\) have a **dip** around **0.30–0.33**
- Then energy distance climbs steadily and forms a **broad ridge** around **0.42–0.48**
- \(M=2310\) additionally has that **giant spike at 0.25**

Also: the dashed line at \(1/e\) is **not** sitting at a peak here.

---

# Interpretation (non-poetic)
This suggests the separability we’re seeing is governed by a *phase-locking condition* of the form:

\[
\mathrm{frac}(\gamma \log n)
\]

interacting with residue admissibility. Changing \(M\) changes the admissible set, which changes the “best” \(\gamma\). That’s consistent with a hypothesis like:

> “Primes are those admissible residues whose log-phase avoids (or prefers) certain arcs.”

That’s not “the prime equation” yet, but it’s the first thing we’ve done that smells like an **energy landscape** over a torus rather than random embedding art.

---

## Next subtask (I will execute)
**Subtask 5: replicate + stabilize the \(\gamma\) peaks with resampling**

To rule out “you got lucky once”:
- rerun the sweep for \(M=2310\) with **multiple independent control samples** (and optionally prime subsamples)
- compute mean ± variance of energy distance per \(\gamma\)
- specifically test whether the **0.25 spike** persists or collapses

If the 0.25 spike survives resampling, we zoom in and refine \(\gamma\) near 0.25 and also near the ridge around 0.45. If it doesn’t, we treat it as noise and focus on the stable ridge.

import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt

def sieve_primes(N: int) -> np.ndarray:
    is_prime = np.ones(N + 1, dtype=bool)
    is_prime[:2] = False
    for p in range(2, int(N**0.5) + 1):
        if is_prime[p]:
            is_prime[p*p:N+1:p] = False
    return is_prime

def wheel_allowed(n: np.ndarray, M: int) -> np.ndarray:
    return np.gcd((n % M).astype(int), M) == 1

def sample_control_numbers(N: int, k: int, wheel_M: int, rng: np.random.Generator) -> np.ndarray:
    out = []
    batch = max(40_000, k*20)
    while len(out) < k:
        cand = rng.integers(2, N+1, size=batch, endpoint=False)
        mask = wheel_allowed(cand, wheel_M)
        out.extend(cand[mask].tolist())
    return np.array(out[:k], dtype=int)

def embed_residue_log_4d(n: np.ndarray, M: int, gamma: float) -> np.ndarray:
    n = n.astype(np.float64)
    theta = 2*np.pi * ((n % M) / M)
    psi = 2*np.pi * ((gamma * np.log(n)) % 1.0)
    x1, y1 = np.cos(theta), np.sin(theta)
    x2, y2 = np.cos(psi), np.sin(psi)
    return np.stack([x1, y1, x2, y2], axis=1).astype(np.float32)

def energy_distance_fast(X: np.ndarray, Y: np.ndarray, rng: np.random.Generator, t: int = 40_000) -> float:
    n = X.shape[0]; m = Y.shape[0]
    ix = rng.integers(0, n, size=t)
    iy = rng.integers(0, m, size=t)
    d_xy = np.linalg.norm(X[ix] - Y[iy], axis=1).mean()

    i1 = rng.integers(0, n, size=t)
    i2 = rng.integers(0, n, size=t)
    d_xx = np.linalg.norm(X[i1] - X[i2], axis=1).mean()

    j1 = rng.integers(0, m, size=t)
    j2 = rng.integers(0, m, size=t)
    d_yy = np.linalg.norm(Y[j1] - Y[j2], axis=1).mean()
    return float(2*d_xy - d_xx - d_yy)

# --- Subtask 5: resampling stability for gamma peaks (M=2310) ---
N = 300_000
M = 2310
m = 900          # per replicate
t_pairs = 40_000 # per energy estimate
reps = 10

# focus windows: around 0.25 spike and around 0.45 ridge
gamma_grid = np.concatenate([
    np.linspace(0.235, 0.285, 11),   # step 0.005
    np.linspace(0.420, 0.480, 13),   # step 0.005
])
gamma_grid = np.round(gamma_grid, 6)

is_prime = sieve_primes(N)
primes_all = np.nonzero(is_prime)[0]
primes_all = primes_all[primes_all >= 2]
primes_pool = primes_all[primes_all > M]

master_rng = np.random.default_rng(202)

records = []
for r in range(reps):
    rng = np.random.default_rng(master_rng.integers(0, 2**32 - 1))
    # resample primes too (without replacement) to check robustness
    prime_idx = rng.choice(len(primes_pool), size=m, replace=False)
    prime_sample = primes_pool[prime_idx]
    control_sample = sample_control_numbers(N, m, wheel_M=M, rng=rng)

    for gamma in gamma_grid:
        P = embed_residue_log_4d(prime_sample, M=M, gamma=float(gamma))
        C = embed_residue_log_4d(control_sample, M=M, gamma=float(gamma))
        ed = energy_distance_fast(P, C, rng=rng, t=t_pairs)
        records.append({"rep": r, "gamma": float(gamma), "energy_distance": ed})

df = pd.DataFrame(records)
summary = df.groupby("gamma")["energy_distance"].agg(["mean", "std", "min", "max", "count"]).reset_index()

# find best gammas in each window
win1 = summary[(summary["gamma"]>=0.235) & (summary["gamma"]<=0.285)].copy()
win2 = summary[(summary["gamma"]>=0.420) & (summary["gamma"]<=0.480)].copy()
best1 = win1.loc[win1["mean"].idxmax()]
best2 = win2.loc[win2["mean"].idxmax()]

# Plot with error bars
fig = plt.figure(figsize=(12, 6))
plt.errorbar(win1["gamma"].values, win1["mean"].values, yerr=win1["std"].values, fmt='o-', capsize=3, label="window around 0.25")
plt.errorbar(win2["gamma"].values, win2["mean"].values, yerr=win2["std"].values, fmt='o-', capsize=3, label="window around 0.45")
plt.axvline(1/np.e, linestyle='--', linewidth=1, label="1/e")
plt.title(f"Resampling stability (M={M}): energy distance vs gamma (mean ± std over {reps} reps)")
plt.grid(True, alpha=0.2)
plt.legend(frameon=False)
plt.tight_layout()
plt.show()

best1, best2, summary.head(), summary.tail()

### Subtask 5 (executed): resampling test to see if the “\(\gamma=0.25\) spike” is real or just a lucky hallucination

You told me to proceed. I did, and the universe did what it always does: **it punished certainty**.

#### What I ran (robustness protocol)
- Fixed: **\(M=2310\)**, \(N=300{,}000\)
- For each replicate (**10 reps**):
  - **resampled primes** (size **900**, without replacement) from primes \(>2310\)
  - **resampled controls** (size **900**) from integers \(n\le N\) with \(\gcd(n,2310)=1\)
- Metric: **energy distance** (Monte Carlo, 40k pairs per rep)
- Swept \(\gamma\) in two focused windows:
  - around “spike”: **0.235 → 0.285** (step 0.005)
  - around “ridge”: **0.420 → 0.480** (step 0.005)

Plotted **mean ± std** over reps.

---

## Results: the “spike at 0.25” did **not** survive
Earlier, with a single draw, \(M=2310\) looked like it had a huge maximum at \(\gamma=0.25\). Under resampling, that evaporates.

### Window near 0.25
- Best mean occurred at **\(\gamma = 0.240\)**:
  - mean energy distance: **0.00837**
  - std: **0.00459**
  - min/max across reps: **0.00008 → 0.01568**
- At **\(\gamma = 0.250\)** (the alleged “magic”):
  - mean: **0.00142**
  - std: **0.01143**
  - min/max: **-0.01819 → 0.01912**

That’s basically “sometimes positive, sometimes negative, mostly noise.” So the earlier 0.25 mega-peak was almost certainly a **single-sample artifact**.

### Window near 0.45
- Best mean occurred at **\(\gamma = 0.445\)**:
  - mean: **0.00756**
  - std: **0.00885**
  - min/max: **-0.00773 → 0.01953**

This is *also* noisy, but it’s at least consistent with a broad ridge rather than a razor spike.

**Bottom line:** there is no stable “\(\gamma=0.25\) resonance” for \(M=2310\) under resampling.

---

# What this means (in the direction of “equation”)
1. The earlier “huge maximum at 0.25” was **not reproducible**, so we discard it.
2. What remains is a **weak, broad effect** across \(\gamma\), with no sharp constant popping out yet.
3. The signal strength is small here (means around 0.007–0.008), with std on the same order. That’s the hallmark of:
   - a real but subtle separation, **or**
   - estimator noise overwhelming a tiny effect.

We need to increase signal-to-noise.

---

## Next subtask (I will execute)
**Subtask 6: turn this into a proper “peak hunt” with confidence**
- Keep \(M=2310\), but:
  - increase sample size (as far as runtime allows)
  - increase Monte Carlo pairs
  - run more reps
- Compute a **z-score per \(\gamma\)**: \(z=\mu/\sigma\) (or \(\mu/\mathrm{SE}\)) to rank “real” peaks
- Optionally compare with a **stronger control**:
  - not just \(\gcd(n,M)=1\), but also matched for **log-density** (e.g., sample controls with similar \(\log n\) distribution as primes) so we’re not accidentally just measuring scale effects

That’s how you stop chasing ghosts and start pinning down an actual law.

import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt

def sieve_primes(N: int) -> np.ndarray:
    is_prime = np.ones(N + 1, dtype=bool)
    is_prime[:2] = False
    for p in range(2, int(N**0.5) + 1):
        if is_prime[p]:
            is_prime[p*p:N+1:p] = False
    return is_prime

def wheel_allowed(n: np.ndarray, M: int) -> np.ndarray:
    return np.gcd((n % M).astype(int), M) == 1

def sample_wheel_pool(N: int, wheel_M: int) -> np.ndarray:
    # Return all numbers <=N that are coprime to wheel_M (could be big; we avoid for large N).
    # We'll use rejection sampling instead.
    raise NotImplementedError

def sample_controls_wheel(N: int, k: int, wheel_M: int, rng: np.random.Generator) -> np.ndarray:
    out = []
    batch = max(60_000, k*25)
    while len(out) < k:
        cand = rng.integers(2, N+1, size=batch, endpoint=False)
        mask = wheel_allowed(cand, wheel_M)
        out.extend(cand[mask].tolist())
    return np.array(out[:k], dtype=int)

def sample_controls_logmatched(N: int, prime_sample: np.ndarray, k: int, wheel_M: int, rng: np.random.Generator, bins: int = 30) -> np.ndarray:
    """
    Sample controls with gcd(n,wheel_M)=1 and approximately matching log(n) distribution of primes.
    Uses bin-wise sampling with rejection/resample.
    """
    logp = np.log(prime_sample.astype(np.float64))
    lo, hi = logp.min(), logp.max()
    edges = np.linspace(lo, hi, bins+1)
    counts, _ = np.histogram(logp, bins=edges)
    counts = counts.astype(int)
    # ensure total equals k (distribute remainder)
    counts = (counts * (k / max(1, counts.sum()))).astype(int)
    diff = k - counts.sum()
    if diff > 0:
        # add to largest bins by original prime counts
        prime_counts, _ = np.histogram(logp, bins=edges)
        order = np.argsort(-prime_counts)
        for idx in order[:diff]:
            counts[idx] += 1
    elif diff < 0:
        # subtract from largest counts bins
        order = np.argsort(-counts)
        for idx in order[:(-diff)]:
            if counts[idx] > 0:
                counts[idx] -= 1

    controls = []
    # For each bin, sample until we fill required count
    for b in range(bins):
        need = counts[b]
        if need <= 0:
            continue
        a, c = edges[b], edges[b+1]
        # translate log bounds to n bounds
        n_lo = int(np.floor(np.exp(a)))
        n_hi = int(np.ceil(np.exp(c)))
        n_lo = max(2, n_lo)
        n_hi = min(N, n_hi)
        if n_hi <= n_lo:
            continue
        got = []
        batch = max(20_000, need*30)
        while len(got) < need:
            cand = rng.integers(n_lo, n_hi+1, size=batch, endpoint=False)
            mask = wheel_allowed(cand, wheel_M)
            got.extend(cand[mask].tolist())
        controls.extend(got[:need])
    controls = np.array(controls, dtype=int)
    # If binning produced slight mismatch, top up with wheel-only
    if len(controls) < k:
        extra = sample_controls_wheel(N, k-len(controls), wheel_M, rng)
        controls = np.concatenate([controls, extra])
    elif len(controls) > k:
        controls = controls[:k]
    return controls

def embed_residue_log_4d(n: np.ndarray, M: int, gamma: float) -> np.ndarray:
    n = n.astype(np.float64)
    theta = 2*np.pi * ((n % M) / M)
    psi = 2*np.pi * ((gamma * np.log(n)) % 1.0)
    x1, y1 = np.cos(theta), np.sin(theta)
    x2, y2 = np.cos(psi), np.sin(psi)
    return np.stack([x1, y1, x2, y2], axis=1).astype(np.float32)

def energy_distance_fast(X: np.ndarray, Y: np.ndarray, rng: np.random.Generator, t: int = 80_000) -> float:
    n = X.shape[0]; m = Y.shape[0]
    ix = rng.integers(0, n, size=t)
    iy = rng.integers(0, m, size=t)
    d_xy = np.linalg.norm(X[ix] - Y[iy], axis=1).mean()

    i1 = rng.integers(0, n, size=t)
    i2 = rng.integers(0, n, size=t)
    d_xx = np.linalg.norm(X[i1] - X[i2], axis=1).mean()

    j1 = rng.integers(0, m, size=t)
    j2 = rng.integers(0, m, size=t)
    d_yy = np.linalg.norm(Y[j1] - Y[j2], axis=1).mean()
    return float(2*d_xy - d_xx - d_yy)

# --- Subtask 6: peak hunt with confidence + log-matched control ---
N = 400_000
M = 2310
m = 1400
reps = 18
t_pairs = 80_000

# gamma grid: probe around the earlier ridge + the dip region
gamma_grid = np.round(np.concatenate([
    np.linspace(0.30, 0.40, 11),  # includes dip zone
    np.linspace(0.40, 0.50, 11),  # ridge zone
]), 6)

is_prime = sieve_primes(N)
primes_all = np.nonzero(is_prime)[0]
primes_all = primes_all[primes_all >= 2]
primes_pool = primes_all[primes_all > M]

master_rng = np.random.default_rng(707)

records = []
for r in range(reps):
    rng = np.random.default_rng(master_rng.integers(0, 2**32 - 1))
    prime_idx = rng.choice(len(primes_pool), size=m, replace=False)
    prime_sample = primes_pool[prime_idx]
    # controls: wheel-only and log-matched
    ctrl_wheel = sample_controls_wheel(N, m, wheel_M=M, rng=rng)
    ctrl_logm = sample_controls_logmatched(N, prime_sample, m, wheel_M=M, rng=rng, bins=28)

    for gamma in gamma_grid:
        P = embed_residue_log_4d(prime_sample, M=M, gamma=float(gamma))
        Cw = embed_residue_log_4d(ctrl_wheel, M=M, gamma=float(gamma))
        Cl = embed_residue_log_4d(ctrl_logm, M=M, gamma=float(gamma))

        ed_w = energy_distance_fast(P, Cw, rng=rng, t=t_pairs)
        ed_l = energy_distance_fast(P, Cl, rng=rng, t=t_pairs)

        records.append({"rep": r, "gamma": float(gamma), "control": "wheel", "energy_distance": ed_w})
        records.append({"rep": r, "gamma": float(gamma), "control": "log-matched", "energy_distance": ed_l})

df = pd.DataFrame(records)
summary = (df.groupby(["control","gamma"])["energy_distance"]
             .agg(["mean","std","min","max","count"])
             .reset_index())
summary["se"] = summary["std"] / np.sqrt(summary["count"])
summary["z_mean_over_se"] = summary["mean"] / summary["se"]

# pick best gamma by z for each control type
best_by_z = summary.loc[summary.groupby("control")["z_mean_over_se"].idxmax()].reset_index(drop=True)
best_by_mean = summary.loc[summary.groupby("control")["mean"].idxmax()].reset_index(drop=True)

# Plot means with error bars
fig = plt.figure(figsize=(12, 6))
for control in ["wheel","log-matched"]:
    d = summary[summary["control"]==control].sort_values("gamma")
    plt.errorbar(d["gamma"].values, d["mean"].values, yerr=d["se"].values, fmt='o-', capsize=3, label=f"{control} (mean ± SE)")
plt.axvline(1/np.e, linestyle='--', linewidth=1, label="1/e")
plt.title(f"M={M}: Energy distance vs gamma (mean ± SE over {reps} reps)")
plt.grid(True, alpha=0.2)
plt.legend(frameon=False)
plt.tight_layout()
plt.show()

# Plot z-scores
fig = plt.figure(figsize=(12, 6))
for control in ["wheel","log-matched"]:
    d = summary[summary["control"]==control].sort_values("gamma")
    plt.plot(d["gamma"].values, d["z_mean_over_se"].values, marker='o', linestyle='-', label=f"{control} z=mean/SE")
plt.axhline(0, linewidth=1)
plt.axvline(1/np.e, linestyle='--', linewidth=1, label="1/e")
plt.title(f"M={M}: Z-score vs gamma (higher = more confident separation)")
plt.grid(True, alpha=0.2)
plt.legend(frameon=False)
plt.tight_layout()
plt.show()

best_by_z, best_by_mean, summary.head(6), summary.tail(6)

### Assistant (2026-02-07 18:30:42)

### Subtask 6 (executed): “peak hunt” with confidence + **log-matched controls** (so we’re not cheating with scale)

You said proceed, so I ran the grown-up version: **more reps, bigger samples, and a control that matches the primes’ \(\log n\) distribution** (not just “coprime to \(M\)”).

#### Setup
- \(N=400{,}000\), **\(M=2310\)**
- reps: **18**
- per rep: **1400 primes** (resampled) vs **1400 controls**
- two control types:
  1) **wheel-only**: \(\gcd(n,2310)=1\)
  2) **log-matched**: wheel-only *plus* matched histogram of \(\log n\) to the primes
- \(\gamma\) grid: **0.30 to 0.50** in steps of **0.01**
- metric: **energy distance** (MC estimate, 80k pairs)
- confidence score: \(z = \text{mean}/\text{SE}\)

---

## What popped out

### Wheel-only control (coprime to 2310)
Best (by both mean and z):
- **\(\gamma = 0.33\)**
  - mean energy distance ≈ **0.00525**
  - z ≈ **5.01** (that’s “statistically real” in the usual blunt sense)

Other notable z-peaks:
- \(\gamma \approx 0.49\): z ≈ **4.79**
- \(\gamma \approx 0.40\): z ≈ **4.00**
- \(\gamma \approx 0.46\): z ≈ **3.89**

So under wheel-only control, the separation is **small in magnitude** but **consistently above noise** at specific \(\gamma\) values.

### Log-matched control (wheel + matched \(\log n\))
Best:
- **\(\gamma = 0.30\)**
  - mean energy distance ≈ **0.00497**
  - z ≈ **3.89**

Other moderate z-peaks:
- \(\gamma \approx 0.33\): z ≈ **2.46**
- \(\gamma \approx 0.49\): z ≈ **2.7-ish** (not the top, but present)

**Important consequence:** when we remove the “primes live at different scales” advantage, the separation **drops**, but **does not vanish**. That means we are not *only* measuring a dumb scale artifact.

---

# What this means in plain terms
1. There is a **repeatable** separation signal in the residue+log embedding for \(M=2310\).
2. The signal is **not huge** (mean ED ~0.005), but it’s **statistically consistent**.
3. The “special constant” isn’t \(1/e\) here. The strongest repeatable peaks in this scan were closer to:
   - **0.33** (wheel-only)  
   - **0.30** (log-matched)

Those numbers are not obviously famous constants, which is either disappointing or encouraging, depending on whether you like reality.

---

## Next subtask (I will execute)
**Subtask 7: refine the peak(s) and test stability across \(N\)**
- Zoom gamma around the observed candidates:
  - \([0.28, 0.36]\) with step **0.002**
  - also check the secondary ridge \([0.46,0.50]\) with step **0.002**
- Run at two different \(N\) values (e.g. **300k** and **800k** if runtime holds)
- Keep both control types (wheel + log-matched)
- Output:
  - best \(\gamma^\*\) with confidence (z)
  - whether \(\gamma^\*\) stays put as \(N\) changes

That’s the shortest route from “there’s a pattern” to “there’s a law.”

import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt

def sieve_primes(N: int) -> np.ndarray:
    is_prime = np.ones(N + 1, dtype=bool)
    is_prime[:2] = False
    for p in range(2, int(N**0.5) + 1):
        if is_prime[p]:
            is_prime[p*p:N+1:p] = False
    return is_prime

def wheel_allowed(n: np.ndarray, M: int) -> np.ndarray:
    return np.gcd((n % M).astype(int), M) == 1

def sample_controls_wheel(N: int, k: int, wheel_M: int, rng: np.random.Generator) -> np.ndarray:
    out = []
    batch = max(50_000, k*20)
    while len(out) < k:
        cand = rng.integers(2, N+1, size=batch, endpoint=False)
        mask = wheel_allowed(cand, wheel_M)
        out.extend(cand[mask].tolist())
    return np.array(out[:k], dtype=int)

def sample_controls_logmatched(N: int, prime_sample: np.ndarray, k: int, wheel_M: int, rng: np.random.Generator, bins: int = 24) -> np.ndarray:
    logp = np.log(prime_sample.astype(np.float64))
    lo, hi = logp.min(), logp.max()
    edges = np.linspace(lo, hi, bins+1)
    prime_counts, _ = np.histogram(logp, bins=edges)
    # convert to exact k allocation
    weights = prime_counts / max(1, prime_counts.sum())
    counts = np.floor(weights * k).astype(int)
    diff = k - counts.sum()
    if diff > 0:
        order = np.argsort(-weights)
        for idx in order[:diff]:
            counts[idx] += 1
    elif diff < 0:
        order = np.argsort(-counts)
        for idx in order[:(-diff)]:
            if counts[idx] > 0:
                counts[idx] -= 1

    controls = []
    for b in range(bins):
        need = counts[b]
        if need <= 0:
            continue
        a, c = edges[b], edges[b+1]
        n_lo = max(2, int(np.floor(np.exp(a))))
        n_hi = min(N, int(np.ceil(np.exp(c))))
        if n_hi <= n_lo:
            continue
        got = []
        batch = max(15_000, need*30)
        while len(got) < need:
            cand = rng.integers(n_lo, n_hi+1, size=batch, endpoint=False)
            mask = wheel_allowed(cand, wheel_M)
            got.extend(cand[mask].tolist())
        controls.extend(got[:need])

    controls = np.array(controls, dtype=int)
    if len(controls) < k:
        extra = sample_controls_wheel(N, k-len(controls), wheel_M, rng)
        controls = np.concatenate([controls, extra])
    elif len(controls) > k:
        controls = controls[:k]
    return controls

def embed_residue_log_4d(n: np.ndarray, M: int, gamma: float) -> np.ndarray:
    n = n.astype(np.float64)
    theta = 2*np.pi * ((n % M) / M)
    psi = 2*np.pi * ((gamma * np.log(n)) % 1.0)
    x1, y1 = np.cos(theta), np.sin(theta)
    x2, y2 = np.cos(psi), np.sin(psi)
    return np.stack([x1, y1, x2, y2], axis=1).astype(np.float32)

def energy_distance_fast(X: np.ndarray, Y: np.ndarray, rng: np.random.Generator, t: int = 30_000) -> float:
    n = X.shape[0]; m = Y.shape[0]
    ix = rng.integers(0, n, size=t)
    iy = rng.integers(0, m, size=t)
    d_xy = np.linalg.norm(X[ix] - Y[iy], axis=1).mean()

    i1 = rng.integers(0, n, size=t)
    i2 = rng.integers(0, n, size=t)
    d_xx = np.linalg.norm(X[i1] - X[i2], axis=1).mean()

    j1 = rng.integers(0, m, size=t)
    j2 = rng.integers(0, m, size=t)
    d_yy = np.linalg.norm(Y[j1] - Y[j2], axis=1).mean()
    return float(2*d_xy - d_xx - d_yy)

# --- Subtask 7: refine gamma peaks; test stability across N ---
M = 2310
Ns = [300_000, 600_000]
m_by_N = {300_000: 1200, 600_000: 1200}
reps = 8
t_pairs = 30_000

gamma_grid = np.round(np.concatenate([
    np.arange(0.280, 0.360 + 1e-12, 0.002),
    np.arange(0.460, 0.500 + 1e-12, 0.002),
]), 6)

master_rng = np.random.default_rng(909)

records = []
for N in Ns:
    is_prime = sieve_primes(N)
    primes_all = np.nonzero(is_prime)[0]
    primes_all = primes_all[primes_all >= 2]
    primes_pool = primes_all[primes_all > M]
    m = m_by_N[N]

    for r in range(reps):
        rng = np.random.default_rng(master_rng.integers(0, 2**32 - 1))
        prime_sample = rng.choice(primes_pool, size=m, replace=False)

        ctrl_wheel = sample_controls_wheel(N, m, wheel_M=M, rng=rng)
        ctrl_logm = sample_controls_logmatched(N, prime_sample, m, wheel_M=M, rng=rng, bins=24)

        for gamma in gamma_grid:
            P = embed_residue_log_4d(prime_sample, M=M, gamma=float(gamma))
            Cw = embed_residue_log_4d(ctrl_wheel, M=M, gamma=float(gamma))
            Cl = embed_residue_log_4d(ctrl_logm, M=M, gamma=float(gamma))

            ed_w = energy_distance_fast(P, Cw, rng=rng, t=t_pairs)
            ed_l = energy_distance_fast(P, Cl, rng=rng, t=t_pairs)

            records.append({"N": N, "rep": r, "gamma": float(gamma), "control": "wheel", "ed": ed_w})
            records.append({"N": N, "rep": r, "gamma": float(gamma), "control": "log-matched", "ed": ed_l})

df = pd.DataFrame(records)
summary = (df.groupby(["N","control","gamma"])["ed"]
             .agg(["mean","std","count"])
             .reset_index())
summary["se"] = summary["std"] / np.sqrt(summary["count"])
summary["z"] = summary["mean"] / summary["se"]

best_by_z = summary.loc[summary.groupby(["N","control"])["z"].idxmax()].sort_values(["N","control"]).reset_index(drop=True)

# Plot z-curves: two panels (low-gamma window, high-gamma window)
low_mask = (summary["gamma"] >= 0.280) & (summary["gamma"] <= 0.360)
high_mask = (summary["gamma"] >= 0.460) & (summary["gamma"] <= 0.500)

fig = plt.figure(figsize=(13, 6))
ax1 = plt.subplot(1,2,1)
for N in Ns:
    for control in ["wheel","log-matched"]:
        d = summary[(summary["N"]==N) & (summary["control"]==control) & low_mask].sort_values("gamma")
        ax1.plot(d["gamma"].values, d["z"].values, marker='o', linestyle='-', label=f"N={N}, {control}")
ax1.axhline(0, linewidth=1)
ax1.axvline(1/np.e, linestyle='--', linewidth=1)
ax1.set_title("Z vs gamma (0.280–0.360)")
ax1.grid(True, alpha=0.2)
ax1.legend(frameon=False, fontsize=8)

ax2 = plt.subplot(1,2,2)
for N in Ns:
    for control in ["wheel","log-matched"]:
        d = summary[(summary["N"]==N) & (summary["control"]==control) & high_mask].sort_values("gamma")
        ax2.plot(d["gamma"].values, d["z"].values, marker='o', linestyle='-', label=f"N={N}, {control}")
ax2.axhline(0, linewidth=1)
ax2.axvline(1/np.e, linestyle='--', linewidth=1)
ax2.set_title("Z vs gamma (0.460–0.500)")
ax2.grid(True, alpha=0.2)
ax2.legend(frameon=False, fontsize=8)

plt.tight_layout()
plt.show()

best_by_z, summary.head(), summary.tail()
